## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves determining the rate law for a chemical reaction, where dA_dt (rate of concentration change) depends on the current concentration A and possibly time t. Classical kinetics dictates that reaction rates follow power-law, rational, or exponential dependencies on concentration.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reactions with equilibrium)
- Competitive inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (substrate inhibition kinetics)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (combination of first and second order)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (product-catalyzed reaction)
- Time-dependent decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-modulated first-order kinetics)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed bimolecular reaction)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 (multiple simultaneous pathways)
- Sigmoidal rate: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative or Hill-type kinetics)
- Exponential decay rate: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * A) (exponential dependence on concentration)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative proportionality to concentration → first-order decay: dA_dt = -k*A, characteristic of radioactive decay and simple decomposition
- Rate depending on concentration squared or higher powers → bimolecular or higher-order elementary reactions
- Rational functions of concentration (A/(K+A)) → enzyme kinetics or surface-catalyzed reactions with site saturation
- Constant offset in rate expression → presence of a reverse reaction or external feed/source term driving toward equilibrium
- Explicit time dependence in rate law → non-autonomous system suggesting external forcing, photolysis, or catalyst deactivation
- Product of concentration terms with opposite signs → competing forward and backward reactions (reversible kinetics)
- Square root dependence on concentration (A**0.5) → chain reaction mechanisms with termination steps
- Logarithmic dependence on concentration → Elovich-type kinetics common in heterogeneous catalysis and chemisorption
- Rate expression with polynomial numerator and denominator in A → complex catalytic mechanisms derived from quasi-steady-state approximations

For any candidate to match GT, it must contain `sin(sqrt(A))` or an equivalent. Since `sin(sqrt(A))` is linearly independent from all polynomial, exponential, logarithmic, and power-law basis functions, no combination of such functions can exactly equal `sin(sqrt(A))` for all A ≥ 0.

**Candidates 26, 27, 32:** These have `sin(c*log(A*c + 1) + c)`. Can `c*log(A*c + 1)` equal `sqrt(A)`? No — `log` and `sqrt` are fundamentally different functions (linearly independent). So these don't match either.

**All other candidates** use combinations of: `A^p`, `exp(A*c)`, `exp(c*t)`, `log(A*c+1)`, `sqrt(A)`, `A^(1/3)`, rational functions — none of which can produce `sin(sqrt(A))`.
